archaeologists found when they discovered their interlocked skeletons.</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span style="font-size: 14.3999996185303px;">The mother is believed to have been trying to protect her child during a powerful earthquake that hit Qinghai province, central China, in about 2,000 BC.</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span style="font-size: 14.3999996185303px;">The remains were dug up on an early Bronze Age archaeological site branded the 'Pompeii of the East', the <a style="font-weight: bold;" class="" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="http://en.people.cn/n/2015/0808/c98649-8933336.html">People's Daily Online</a> reported. </span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span style="font-size: 14.3999996185303px;"><span   </script> </div> </div> </div><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span style="font-size: 14.3999996185303px;">The incredibly well-preserved site paints a tragic picture of people trying to their families in the midst of a terrifying earthquake.</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span style="font-size: 14.3999996185303px;">The Lajia site is the largest disaster excavation site in China at nearly 40,000 square feet and was first discovered in the early 2000s. </span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span style="font-size: 14.3999996185303px;">The excavation site is of particular historical importance because it holds clues to an early Bronze Age civilisation that lived in the upper Yellow River region. The team of archaeologists presented their findings at an academic conference in Gansu province, northwest China, earlier this month.</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span style="font-size: 14.3999996185303px;">The skeletons are now on display at the Lajia Ruins Museum.</span></p><div class="art-ins mol-factbox news" data-permabox-url="https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/peoplesdaily/article-3192196/Enduring-love-4-000-year-old-skeletons-mother-child-locked-dying-embrace-Pompeii-East.html"> <h3 class="wocc"><b>THE BODIES OF THOSE WHO DIED WHEN VESUVIUS ENGULFED POMPEII </b></h3> <div class="ins cleared xolcc bdrcc"><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"><span class="mol-style-bold">Experts have been working on the carefully preserved plaster casts of Romans trapped in Pompeii in 79 AD following the deadly eruption of Mount Vesuvius.</span></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"><span class="mol-style-bold">The victims have been entombed in ash for nearly 2,000 years and include what appears to be a mother with a child resting on her stomach.</span></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"><span class="mol-style-bold">The poses of the bodies reveal how they died, some trapped in buildings and others sheltering with family members.</span><span class="mol-style-bold"> </span></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"><span class="mol-style-bold">Mount Vesuvius erupted on August 24, spewing ash hundreds of feet into the air for 18 hours.</span></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"><span class="mol-style-bold">But the deadly disaster occurred the next morning, when the volcano’s cone collapsed, causing an avalanche of mud travelling at 100mph to flood Pompeii.</span></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"><span class="mol-style-bold">People were buried too in the ash, which hardened to form a porous shell, meaning that the soft tissues of the bodies decayed, leaving the skeleton in a void.</span></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"><span class="mol-style-bold">Reports claim 2,000 people died, and the location was abandoned until it was rediscovered in 1748.</span></font></p><div class="mol-img-group xwArtSplitter"> <div class="mol-img"> <div class="image-wrap"> <img id="i-bd44731b89b67c88" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/08/10/18/2B3FAF5500000578-3192196-Bodies_of_Pompeii_Remains_entombed_in_ash_show_a_young_child_res-a-12_1439229534205.jpg" height="629" width="952" alt="Bodies of Pompeii: Remains entombed in ash show a young child resting on the stomach of an adult " class="blkBorder img-share" style="max-width:100%" loading="lazy" /> </div> <noscript> <img id="i-bd44731b89b67c88" src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/08/10/18/2B3FAF5500000578-3192196-Bodies_of_Pompeii_Remains_entombed_in_ash_show_a_young_child_res-a-12_1439229534205.jpg" height="629" width="952" alt="Bodies of Pompeii: Remains entombed in ash show a young child resting on the stomach of an adult " class="blkBorder img-share" /> </noscript> </div> <p class="imageCaption">Bodies of Pompeii: Remains entombed in ash show a young child resting on the stomach of an adult </p></div><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size:1.2em"></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"></p></div> </div><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size: 1.2em"></font></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font style="font-size: 1.2em"></font></p></div>
